Artists chosen for their originality and vision will do performances largely made up of premieres or improvisations the ears might not be accustomed to, but the audience are rewarded with one of a kind-musical moments.\n\n3.30-4.20 p.m.: Christian Vuust + Buchanan/Held/Eilertsen/Norbakken\n\nChristian Vuust explores the Nordic tone in jazz music and will also draw from the European sound at Ujazz where he has gathered a group of stellar musicians including Jakob Buchanan (trumpet), Pablo Held (keys), Mats Eilertsen (bass) and Helge Norbakken (perc.). Christian Vuust was nominated in the category jazz composer of the year at the 2014 Danish Music Awards.\n\n4.30-5.00 p.m.: Homies x Hoiness\n\nThe trio consisting of Ned Ferm (sax), Jeppe Skovbakke (bass) and Rune Kielsgaard (drums) create their own sound with what they call action-drone inspired improvisations. They met in the internationally acclaimed group Anderskov Accident in 2001 and have since played together with various artists. At Ujazz they will be accompanied by top guitarist Oliver Hoiness.\n\n5.10-5.50 p.m.: Stefano Bollani & Diego Schissi\n\nTwo of today’s most interesting jazz pianists join forces at this show. Italian Stefano Bollani floats effortlessly in and out of classical music, jazz and everything in between while Diego Schissi displays musical supremacy by evolving Argentinian tango in new directions. Combine the two and you have a duo who has played all around the world and with the biggest names in jazz.\n\n6.00-6.20 p.m.: Illdjinn\n\nVersatile drummer Mads Forsby has been underway with his solo project for some time and is now ready to present Illdjinn. Solo improvisations and the drum kit equipped with special microphones and triggers to synthesizers are the foundation of his sound where he mixes a more traditional approach to improvisational music with a modern, electronic sampling mentality.\n\n6.30-7.00 p.m.: Jacob Anderkovs Strings, Percussion & Piano\n\nIn ‘Strings, Percussion & Piano’ Anderskov combines the composed with the improvised. The strings bring out a poetic beauty in the music that collides perfectly with the improvisations of Peter Bruun (drums) and Jacob Anderskov (keys). The string trio consists of Christine Pryn (violin), Anette Slaatto (viola) and Ida Nørholm (cello).\n\n7.10-7.50 p.m.: The Wild Mans Band\n\nThree legends in improvisational music make up The Wild Mans Band who have played numerous shows in Scandinavia and Germany. Peter Brötzmann’s horns move from the explosive to the lingering and back. Deeper in the mix Peter Friis-Nielsen’s bass and Peter Ole Jørgensen’s drums create a rhythmic base and drives the music on musical detours for the band to explore.\n\n8.00-8.45 p.m.: Howe Gelb: Deconstructing standards feat. Steve Shelley & Yasmine Hamdan\n\nHowe Gelb is a master of ripping his own songs apart and putting them together in new ways with sudden and unexpected dissonant beauty as result. At Ujazz we have asked him to deconstruct jazz standards with Sonic Youth-drummer Steve Shelley and Lebanese singer Yasmine Hamdan. And whoever Howe might meet on his way.\n\n10.30-11.30 p.m.: Fire! Orchestra\n\nSwedish band Fire! have established themselves as a great artist in freejazz, but they are not shy to explore garage rock, krautrock and electronica as well. With Fire! Orchestra they expand to 18-man orchestra and experiment with both the sound and the big band-format. Inspired by the likes of Charlie Haden, Carla Bley and Sun Ra they add their own boundary pushing mentality.\n\nDoors open at 3. Arrive to the shows early as there is limited space.\n\nDuring Ujazz, Ujazz+ will take place 9.00-10.30 p.m. at VoxHall with Daniel Lanois.\n\nCanadian singer, guitarist and producer has worked with great artists such as Bob Dylan, Emmylou Harris and Peter Gabriel and is celebrated for his work with Brian Eno on some of U2’s biggest albums where they created new standards in ambient music. As an artist of his own Daniel Lanois’ expressive playing and profound storytelling have resulted in several albums. At Ujazz+ he will be performing with songs from his newest album ‘Flesh and Machine’ on which he uses a mix of organic sounds and electronically manipulated elements in an unconventional way.\n\nTickets to Daniel Lanois are sold seperately. Lund to the Northwest coast of Denmark to spend one week recording in a secluded farmhouse with the Danish portion of Giant Sand as the backing band.
